<p><b>Queen Silvia of Sweden</b> (<small>Swedish pronunciation: </small><span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Swedish" title="Help:IPA for Swedish">[ˈsɪlvɪa]</a></span>; born <b>Silvia Renate Sommerlath</b> on 23 December 1943) is the spouse of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/King_Carl_XVI_Gustaf" title="King Carl XVI Gustaf">King Carl XVI Gustaf</a> and mother of the <a href="/wiki/Heir_apparent" title="Heir apparent">heir apparent</a> to the throne, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crown_Princess_Victoria" title="Crown Princess Victoria">Crown Princess Victoria</a>. In 2011, Silvia became the longest serving queen of Sweden, a record previously held by <a href="/wiki/Sophia_of_Nassau" title="Sophia of Nassau">Sophia of Nassau</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Childhood_and_parentage">Childhood and parentage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen_Silvia_of_Sweden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Childhood and parentage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Silvia Renate Sommerlath was born in <a href="/wiki/Heidelberg" title="Heidelberg">Heidelberg</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Germany</a>, on 23 December 1943,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> the only daughter of the late <a href="/wiki/Alice_Sommerlath" title="Alice Sommerlath">Alice</a> (née Soares de Toledo) and <a href="/wiki/Walther_Sommerlath" title="Walther Sommerlath">Walther Sommerlath</a>. Her father was German and her mother was Brazilian.</p>
<p>She has two older brothers: Ralf and Walther Sommerlath. They and their families were guests at the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Wedding_of_Victoria,_Crown_Princess_of_Sweden,_and_Daniel_Westling" title="Wedding of Victoria, Crown Princess of Sweden, and Daniel Westling">wedding of Victoria, Crown Princess of Sweden, and Daniel Westling</a> <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Wedding_of_Princess_Madeleine_and_Christopher_O%27Neill" title="Wedding of Princess Madeleine and Christopher O'Neill">wedding of Princess Madeleine</a> in 2013. Her third brother, Jörg Sommerlath, died in 2006. The Mother-Child House Jörg Sommerlath in Berlin, operated by Queen Silvia's World Childhood Foundation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> is named after him.</p>
<p>The Sommerlath family lived in <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Paulo" title="São Paulo">São Paulo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, between 1947 and 1957, where the Queen attended the traditional German school <a href="/wiki/Col%C3%A9gio_Visconde_de_Porto_Seguro" title="Colégio Visconde de Porto Seguro">Colégio Visconde de Porto Seguro</a> and Walther Sommerlath held various positions, including President of the Brazilian subsidiary of Swedish company <a href="/wiki/Uddeholms_AB" title="Uddeholms AB">Uddeholms AB</a>. The family returned to <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">West Germany</a> in 1957.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen_Silvia_of_Sweden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-BLP_sources" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><img alt="" data-file-height="40" data-file-width="40" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section of a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Biographies_of_living_persons" title="Wikipedia:Biographies of living persons">biography of a living person</a> <b>needs additional <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">citations</a> for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help by adding <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources">reliable sources</a>. Contentious material about living persons that is unsourced or poorly sourced <b>must be removed immediately</b>, especially if potentially <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Libel" title="Wikipedia:Libel">libelous</a> or harmful.</span> <small><i>(April 2016)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Before her marriage to the King of Sweden, Silvia Sommerlath worked at the <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentine</a> Consulate in Munich, was an educational host during the <a href="/wiki/1972_Summer_Olympics" title="1972 Summer Olympics">1972 Summer Olympics</a> in Munich, and served as the Deputy Head of Protocol for the <a href="/wiki/1976_Winter_Olympics" title="1976 Winter Olympics">Winter Games in Innsbruck</a> in <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> She briefly worked as a <a href="/wiki/Flight_attendant" title="Flight attendant">flight attendant</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>A trained interpreter, <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a> is actually her <a href="/wiki/Multilingualism" title="Multilingualism">sixth language</a>. She speaks her native German, her mother's language of <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>, and <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a>. She has some fluency in <a href="/wiki/Swedish_Sign_Language" title="Swedish Sign Language">Swedish Sign Language</a>, a national sign language used by the <a href="/wiki/Deaf_culture" title="Deaf culture">deaf community</a> in Sweden.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marriage">Marriage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen_Silvia_of_Sweden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Marriage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-BLP_unsourced" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><img alt="" data-file-height="40" data-file-width="40" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></div>

<small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Queen+Silvia+of+Sweden%22&amp;num=50" rel="nofollow">"Queen Silvia of Sweden"</a> – <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?q=%22Queen+Silvia+of+Sweden%22&amp;tbm=nws" rel="nofollow">news</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Queen+Silvia+of+Sweden%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers" rel="nofollow">newspapers</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Queen+Silvia+of+Sweden%22" rel="nofollow">books</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Queen+Silvia+of+Sweden%22" rel="nofollow">scholar</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="http://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Queen+Silvia+of+Sweden%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on" rel="nofollow">JSTOR</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/images?safe=off&amp;tbm=isch&amp;tbs=sur:fmc&amp;q=%22Queen+Silvia+of+Sweden%22+-site:wikipedia.org+-site:wikimedia.org" rel="nofollow">free images</a></span></small></span> <small><i>(April 2016)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/1972_Summer_Olympics" title="1972 Summer Olympics">1972 Summer Olympics</a>, Silvia Sommerlath met Crown Prince Carl Gustaf. In a later interview, the King explained how it just "clicked" when they met. After the death of King <a href="/wiki/Gustaf_VI_Adolf_of_Sweden" title="Gustaf VI Adolf of Sweden">Gustaf VI Adolf</a> on 15 September 1973, Carl XVI Gustaf succeeded to the throne.</p>
<p>He and Silvia announced their engagement on 12 March 1976 and were married three months later, on 19 June in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stockholm_Cathedral" title="Stockholm Cathedral">Stockholm Cathedral</a> ("<a href="/wiki/Storkyrkan" title="Storkyrkan">Storkyrkan</a> Cathedral") in <a href="/wiki/Stockholm" title="Stockholm">Stockholm</a>. It was the first marriage of a reigning Swedish monarch since 1797. If he had married Silvia during the reign of his grandfather, King Gustaf VI Adolf, he would have lost his position as heir-apparent to the Swedish throne. This was due to the inflexibility of his grandfather, who believed that royalty must marry royalty. This was also the reason why Carl Gustaf's uncle, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prince_Bertil" title="Prince Bertil">Prince Bertil</a>, did not marry until after Gustaf VI Adolf's death. (Bertil was second-in-line to the throne until his nephew produced an heir, and was therefore unable to marry the Welsh commoner, <a href="/wiki/Princess_Lilian,_Duchess_of_Halland" title="Princess Lilian, Duchess of Halland">Princess Lilian</a>, with whom he had been in love for decades, until 1976.)</p>
<p>In celebration of the forthcoming wedding of the King and the soon-to-be-Queen, Silvia, the internationally famous pop group <a href="/wiki/ABBA" title="ABBA">ABBA</a> performed the song <i><a href="/wiki/Dancing_Queen" title="Dancing Queen">Dancing Queen</a></i> at a gala performance attended by the King and Silvia the night before the ceremony, although the song was not written for Silvia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The King and Queen of Sweden have three children and five grandchildren.</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Victoria,_Crown_Princess_of_Sweden" title="Victoria, Crown Princess of Sweden">Crown Princess Victoria, Duchess of Västergötland</a> (born 14 July 1977). She is married to <a href="/wiki/Prince_Daniel,_Duke_of_V%C3%A4sterg%C3%B6tland" title="Prince Daniel, Duke of Västergötland">Daniel Westling</a>, and they have a daughter and a son:
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Princess_Estelle,_Duchess_of_%C3%96sterg%C3%B6tland" title="Princess Estelle, Duchess of Östergötland">Princess Estelle, Duchess of Östergötland</a> (born 23 February 2012)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Prince_Oscar,_Duke_of_Sk%C3%A5ne" title="Prince Oscar, Duke of Skåne">Prince Oscar, Duke of Skåne</a> (born 2 March 2016)</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Prince_Carl_Philip,_Duke_of_V%C3%A4rmland" title="Prince Carl Philip, Duke of Värmland">Prince Carl Philip, Duke of Värmland</a> (born 13 May 1979). He is married to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Princess_Sofia,_Duchess_of_Varmland" title="Princess Sofia, Duchess of Varmland">Sofia Hellqvist</a>, and they have a son:
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Prince_Alexander,_Duke_of_S%C3%B6dermanland" title="Prince Alexander, Duke of Södermanland">Prince Alexander, Duke of Södermanland</a> (born 19 April 2016)</li>
</ul>
</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Princess_Madeleine,_Duchess_of_H%C3%A4lsingland_and_G%C3%A4strikland" title="Princess Madeleine, Duchess of Hälsingland and Gästrikland">Princess Madeleine, Duchess of Hälsingland and Gästrikland</a>, (born 10 June 1982). She is married to <a href="/wiki/Christopher_O%27Neill" title="Christopher O'Neill">Christopher O'Neill</a>, and they have a daughter and a son:
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Princess_Leonore,_Duchess_of_Gotland" title="Princess Leonore, Duchess of Gotland">Princess Leonore, Duchess of Gotland</a> (born 20 February 2014)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Prince_Nicolas,_Duke_of_%C3%85ngermanland" title="Prince Nicolas, Duke of Ångermanland">Prince Nicolas, Duke of Ångermanland</a> (born 15 June 2015)</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen_Silvia_of_Sweden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Queen_Silvia_and_Carl_XVI_Gustaf_of_Sweden_in_2015.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="879" data-file-width="856" height="226" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Queen_Silvia_and_Carl_XVI_Gustaf_of_Sweden_in_2015.jpg/220px-Queen_Silvia_and_Carl_XVI_Gustaf_of_Sweden_in_2015.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Queen_Silvia_and_Carl_XVI_Gustaf_of_Sweden_in_2015.jpg/330px-Queen_Silvia_and_Carl_XVI_Gustaf_of_Sweden_in_2015.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/Queen_Silvia_and_Carl_XVI_Gustaf_of_Sweden_in_2015.jpg/440px-Queen_Silvia_and_Carl_XVI_Gustaf_of_Sweden_in_2015.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Queen_Silvia_and_Carl_XVI_Gustaf_of_Sweden_in_2015.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The Queen with the King in 2015.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Despite the initial lukewarm response to a commoner queen, the Swedish press quickly warmed to Queen Silvia and soon began publishing admiring articles about how easily she fit into the country's expectations of queenly deportment. As the Swedish newspaper <i>Svenska Dagbladet</i> noted in 1994, on the occasion of the Queen's 50th birthday, she had revived the popularity of the monarchy. "With Silvia, the republic died. You could put it that way. Even if Silvia's arrival was like kicking someone lying down. Or hitting a guy with glasses. The guy with glasses was mostly to be found with the Social Democrats. A few lines in the party manifesto, ever more vague over the years. It has always been there, but nobody has ever done anything to implement it."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In 2003, Queen Silvia told a Swedish reporter that she and the royal family would like to be more open to contact with magazines and newspapers but that false articles about the family's lives – including photograph montages purported to show the Crown Princess and Princess Madeleine with their "secret" babies, published in the German magazine "Frau mit Herz" – had made them wary. As she told the Swedish news agency TT, "If a person is hurt too much, the natural reaction is to withdraw. That is a pity, because I really think our children are very natural and open toward other people and toward journalists."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Father.27s_Nazi_reported_links">Father's Nazi reported links</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen_Silvia_of_Sweden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Father's Nazi reported links">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-BLP_sources" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><img alt="" data-file-height="40" data-file-width="40" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Biographies_of_living_persons" title="Wikipedia:Biographies of living persons">about a living person</a> <b>needs additional <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">citations</a> for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help by adding <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources">reliable sources</a>. Contentious material about living persons that is unsourced or poorly sourced <b>must be removed immediately</b>, especially if potentially <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Libel" title="Wikipedia:Libel">libelous</a> or harmful.</span> <small><i>(October 2016)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>In 2002, the Queen became the unwelcome subject of international curiosity when an article published in the <a href="/wiki/Central_Organisation_of_the_Workers_of_Sweden" title="Central Organisation of the Workers of Sweden">syndicalist</a> newspaper <a href="/wiki/Arbetaren" title="Arbetaren">Arbetaren</a> reported that German state archives record that the queen's father, <a href="/wiki/Walther_Sommerlath" title="Walther Sommerlath">Walther Sommerlath</a>, joined the Nazi party's foreign wing, the <a href="/wiki/NSDAP/AO" title="NSDAP/AO">NSDAP/AO</a>, in 1934, when he was living in <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a> and working for a German steel company<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rumors had long circulated about Sommerlath's life and career during <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, especially so when his daughter's relationship with the future King of Sweden became known, but until his death in 1990, the businessman denied any connection to the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Party" title="Nazi Party">Nazi Party</a>. However, a study of state records further revealed that Sommerlath, in 1938, through the <a href="/wiki/Aryanization_(Nazism)" title="Aryanization (Nazism)">aryanization</a> policies in effect in Germany at the time, became the owner of a steel factory that "produced components for the German war effort, including parts for Panzers, as well as gas masks," according to the <a href="/wiki/The_Scotsman" title="The Scotsman">Scotsman</a> (20 July 2002). When the revelations about Walther Sommerlath broke in the Swedish press, a palace spokesperson said, "The Queen's father has never been a part of the Royal Family and therefore I have no comment."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In December 2010, she wrote a letter of complaint to <a href="/wiki/Jan_Scherman" title="Jan Scherman">Jan Scherman</a>, the CEO of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TV4_Sweden" title="TV4 Sweden">TV4</a>, the network that had aired a documentary about her father's alleged Nazi past.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p>Queen Silvia commissioned a report from World War II expert Erik Norberg, a choice which was criticized due to Norberg having ties to the Royal Family. In his report, Norberg argued that the Queen's father had in fact helped the owner of the steel-fabrication plant, a Jewish businessperson, escape from Germany by taking over the factory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> In a December 2011 interview for Channel 1 with Sweden's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_service_broadcasting" title="Public service broadcasting">public service</a> broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Sveriges_Television" title="Sveriges Television">Sveriges Television</a>, Silvia called media's handling of the information about her father "<a href="/wiki/Character_assassination" title="Character assassination">character assassination</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Charity_involvement">Charity involvement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen_Silvia_of_Sweden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Charity involvement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-BLP_sources" role="presentation">

<td class="mbox-image">

<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Drottning_Silvia_i_Oslo_juni_2005.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="655" data-file-width="476" height="303" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Drottning_Silvia_i_Oslo_juni_2005.JPG/220px-Drottning_Silvia_i_Oslo_juni_2005.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Drottning_Silvia_i_Oslo_juni_2005.JPG/330px-Drottning_Silvia_i_Oslo_juni_2005.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Drottning_Silvia_i_Oslo_juni_2005.JPG/440px-Drottning_Silvia_i_Oslo_juni_2005.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Drottning_Silvia_i_Oslo_juni_2005.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Queen Silvia in Oslo during the celebration of the 100th anniversary of the <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_the_union_between_Norway_and_Sweden" title="Dissolution of the union between Norway and Sweden">dissolution of the union between Norway and Sweden</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Queen Silvia is involved in numerous <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charity_organization" title="Charity organization">charity organizations</a>, especially in the area of disadvantaged children, and has made several public statements about <a href="/wiki/Human_rights" title="Human rights">human rights</a> and children <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sexual_exploitation" title="Sexual exploitation">sexual exploitation</a>. On her own initiative, she alone watched videos confiscated by the police, of <a href="/wiki/Child_sexual_abuse" title="Child sexual abuse">sexually abused children</a> in an early pedophile tangle. The statement she made to the press became an eye opener for many people that the problem exists.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>She was a co-founder of the <a href="/wiki/World_Childhood_Foundation" title="World Childhood Foundation">World Childhood Foundation</a> in 1999, having been inspired by her work as Patron of the first World Congress against Commercial Sexual Exploitation of Children held in Stockholm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> She has also been involved in the <a href="/wiki/Global_Child_Forum" title="Global Child Forum">Global Child Forum</a>, which she helped initiate, as a keynote speaker in several forums. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup></p>
<p>She works actively for the handicapped, including as Chairman of the Royal Wedding Fund and Queen Silvia's Jubilee Fund. In 1990, she was awarded the prestigious German prize "Deutscher Kulturpreis" for her work for the handicapped. She is an honorary board member of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Mentor_Foundation_International" title="The Mentor Foundation International">The Mentor Foundation International</a>, that works against drug use in adolescents and young adults. She is Patroness of the "Queen Silvia Fund" operated by the <a href="/wiki/World_Scout_Foundation" title="World Scout Foundation">World Scout Foundation</a> which raises funds for Scouts with disabilities.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Her commitment to the work with <a href="/wiki/Dementia" title="Dementia">dementia</a> and the care of the elderly at the end of life is also well known and respected. On her initiative, Silviahemmet was established in Stockholm. It works to educate hospital personnel in how to work with people suffering from dementia, and also initiates research in the area.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Queen also has brought the subject of <a href="/wiki/Dyslexia" title="Dyslexia">dyslexia</a> into the public arena in Sweden. For many years, it was widely rumored that the King has dyslexia. Journalists noted that he misspelled his name when signing his accession document, and in 1973, when visiting a copper mine, he misspelled his name when signing it on a rock wall. In an interview on Swedish television in 1997, the condition was admitted publicly when the Queen addressed the issue. "When he was little, people did not pay attention to the problem," she said. "He didn't get the help he needed."</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="National_honours">National honours</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Queen_Silvia_of_Sweden&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: National honours">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1600" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/23px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/35px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/46px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>: Member Grand Cross of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Order_of_the_Seraphim" title="Royal Order of the Seraphim">Royal Order of the Seraphim</a> (<b>LoK av KMO</b>)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1600" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/23px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/35px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/46px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>: Member of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Family_Order#Sweden" title="Royal Family Order">Royal Family Decoration of King Carl XVI Gustaf, 1st Class</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1600" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/23px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/35px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/46px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>: Recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Jubilee_Commemorative_Medals" title="Royal Jubilee Commemorative Medals">50th Birthday Badge Medal of King Carl XVI Gustaf</a></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1600" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/23px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/35px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/46px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>: Recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Jubilee_Commemorative_Medals" title="Royal Jubilee Commemorative Medals">Wedding Medal of Crown Princess Victoria to Daniel Westling</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><img alt="" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="1000" data-file-width="1600" height="14" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/23px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/35px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/4/4c/Flag_of_Sweden.svg/46px-Flag_of_Sweden.svg.png 2x" width="23"/> </span><a href="/wiki/Sweden" title="Sweden">Sweden</a>: Recipient of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Jubilee_Commemorative_Medals" title="Royal Jubilee Commemorative Medals">Ruby Jubilee Badge Medal of King Carl XVI Gustaf</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></li>
